  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer17632302795746322868">Katarina Bishop has worn a lot of labels in her short life. Friend. Niece. Daughter. Thief.   <span id="freeText17632302795746322868" style="display:none">Katarina Bishop has worn a lot of labels in her short life. Friend. Niece. Daughter. Thief. But for the last two months she’s simply been known as the girl who ran the crew that robbed the greatest museum in the world. That’s why Kat isn’t surprised when she’s asked to steal the infamous Cleopatra Emerald so it can be returned to its rightful owners. <br /><br />There are only three problems. First, the gem hasn’t been seen in public in thirty years. Second, since the fall of the Egyptian empire and the suicide of Cleopatra, no one who holds the emerald keeps it for long, and in Kat’s world, history almost always repeats itself. But it’s the third problem that makes Kat’s crew the most nervous and that is simply… the emerald is cursed.<br /><br />Kat might be in way over her head, but she’s not going down without a fight. After all she has her best friend—the gorgeous Hale—and the rest of her crew with her as they chase the Cleopatra around the globe, dodging curses, realizing that the same tricks and cons her family has used for centuries are useless this time.<br /><br />Which means, this time, Katarina Bishop is making up her own rules.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17632302795746322868" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    He didn't fall because Charlie, his twin, posed as a dead person when it looked like he fell of the edge. Most likely, he had a parachute pack under h<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    He didn't fall because Charlie, his twin, posed as a dead person when it looked like he fell of the edge. Most likely, he had a parachute pack under his shirt. But that's in Perfect Scoundrels, not Uncommon Crimijna!s.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1278267433?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781455815340" href="/book/show/10382265-uncommon-criminals">review of another edition</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=audio">audio</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1278267433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9106842741660958345">This was my very first audiobook!<br/>I'd never found a reason to listen to a book (rather than read it) because it just takes so much longer to finish. Also, I noticed that most people who love audiobooks tend to have a commute, and I'm never in a car (without kids) long enough to listen to anything.<br/>So, no reason for audio books.<br/><b>But.</b><br/>I started exercising...because flab happens. <br/>And for a while, it was fun with Richard.<br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433258292ra/15073052.gif' width='300' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Eventually, however, I moved on to an aerobic walking video. Because I'm cool like</span>
  <span id="freeText9106842741660958345" style="display:none">This was my very first audiobook!<br>I'd never found a reason to listen to a book (rather than read it) because it just takes so much longer to finish. Also, I noticed that most people who love audiobooks tend to have a commute, and I'm never in a car (without kids) long enough to listen to anything.<br>So, no reason for audio books.<br><b>But.</b><br>I started exercising...because flab happens. <br>And for a while, it was fun with Richard.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433258292ra/15073052.gif" width="300" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Eventually, however, I moved on to an aerobic walking video. Because I'm cool like that. And also because it hurts my knees to even <i>watch</i> stuff like this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433264196ra/15074032.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And as much as I benefit from the low impact exercise, the lady who does them is like Fran Drescher in yoga pants.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433265163i/15074202.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Is your workout in a slump? Then come join us! We're sisters in SWEAT!<br><b>{insert braying laugh}</b> This is REAL sweat, ladies! <br>*in fake Italian accent* I lika to sweat! <br><b>{insert more braying laughter}</b> I'm soooo silly!</i><br>God help me, for 45 minutes a day, part of my workout consisted of <b>not</b> throwing my shoe at the television.<br>Then one glorious morning at the library, I was introduced to a little something called <b>Play-A-Way</b>. <br>Not by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1171076-danielle-long" rel="nofollow noopener">My Librarian</a>, mind you. No, she was too busy collecting late fees (<b>probably from orphans!</b>) to bother showing off this technological wonder to an honored patron like myself. <br><i>Not mad, Danielle, just disappointed...</i><br>And now, with tiny things that the kids these days are calling <i>
  <b>earbuds</b>
</i>, I can block the goat-like bleating of Walking Chick's voice, while <i>still</i> making my doctor happy with my daily dose of aerobics, <b>AND</b> I get to listen to a story while I do it!<br><br>So, was <b>Uncommon Criminals</b> any good, you ask?<br>Well...<br>I grabbed it because it was available that day at the library, and not because I'm a big fan of Ally Carter's series.<br>I was just so friggin' happy not to be listening to those lame jokes &amp; horsey laughter that I'm pretty sure I would have enjoyed anything.<br><br>Having said that, I think this was a cute story. Not fantastic, but cute. <br>I had a hard time swallowing that these kids were good enough to fly all around the world and con professionals. But, then again, I'm waaay outside the age range for teeny-bopper heist stories. And this is <i>definitely</i> a teeny-bopper story. I do love YA, but this isn't a series that I would recommend to adult readers.<br>But it <i>is</i> something that I would recommend to my daughter in a year or so, which says something.<br><br><b>Recommended for teens.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="9106842741660958345" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_357885968" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/357885968" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/357885968?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408316221" href="/book/show/15731732-uncommon-criminals">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=own-a-dtb">own-a-dtb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=hachette">hachette</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2012">reviewed-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=just-another-book-crush">just-another-book-crush</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=horrible-whiner">horrible-whiner</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer357885968" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4734677416338669689">If there was ever a Young Adult book written almost exclusively for actual young adults, it’s Uncommon Criminals. In fact, with its light tone, overly simplified plot, short chapters, third person narrative and extremely subtle romance, it is at times more appropriate for younger young adults or even middle grade readers and should be judged/rated as such. <br/><br/>After successfully stealing (back) four paintings from the seemingly impenetrable Henley museum and returning them to their rightful owners, </span>
  <span id="freeText4734677416338669689" style="display:none">If there was ever a Young Adult book written almost exclusively for actual young adults, it’s Uncommon Criminals. In fact, with its light tone, overly simplified plot, short chapters, third person narrative and extremely subtle romance, it is at times more appropriate for younger young adults or even middle grade readers and should be judged/rated as such. <br /><br />After successfully stealing (back) four paintings from the seemingly impenetrable Henley museum and returning them to their rightful owners, Kat has acquired a Robin Hood-like reputation. Therefore, she is only mildly surprised when an old lady, the rightful owner of the Kleopatra emerald, asks her to steal the supposedly cursed stone and return it to her family. Still feeling lucky after several well-done jobs, Kat shuts down her instincts and accepts the job. Hale is the voice of reason, very much against it, but as always, he goes where Kat goes, regardless of the consequences. <br />If Heist Society reminded me a lot of Ocean’s Eleven, Uncommon Criminals is an oversimplified version of Ocean’s Twelve. The crew gets conned by a better thief and they must find a way to outsmart that thief and retrieve what they lost. (Though the thief here isn’t as hot as Vincent Cassel, that’s for sure.)<br /><br />As much as I like Hale (and he’s one swoon-worthy boy, believe me), his wealth and status seem awfully convenient at times. His contacts open all doors, the crew travels in private jets, and if they need a yacht near Monte Carlo, well of course he has one ready! I loved how devoted he was to Kat in Heist Society, but in Uncommon Criminals, he went from being devoted to being a doormat at times. Kat too seems to have changed for the worst. After the Henley job, she developed not just a reputation, but an overabundance of ego as well. She had reason to, up to a point, but she went a bit too far by taking sole credit for something that was a team effort. <br /><br />Keeping in mind what I mentioned at the beginning, I won’t lower my rating because the heists themselves seemed far too simple. I look at this book the same way I’d look at The Famous Five – I would have adored it when I was twelve, loved it still when I was 14. At 28, I found it entertaining, but I really can’t take it seriously. <br /><br />I’ll read the third book mostly because it focuses on Hale, and from all the characters, he’s the one I haven’t managed to figure out. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4734677416338669689" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_174104060" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/174104060" />
    <a title="Nic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2813423-nic"><img alt="Nic" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/174104060?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nic" href="/user/show/2813423-nic">Nic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=so-much-fun">so-much-fun</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer174104060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11519462693472690106"><b>For a bit of W.W. Hale eye candy go to</b> <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://irresistiblereads.blogspot.com/2011/07/my-book-boyfriend-23.html#comments'>http://irresistiblereads.blogspot.com...</a><br/><br/><b>Rating: 4.5</b><br/><br/><b>Favourite Quote:</b> <i>Luck is a strange thing in the life of any thief and halfway decent con man. What is it that keeps the mark from counting the till or the guards from looking up at precisely the wrong moment? Kat had learned at a very young age that luck is for the amateur, the lazy---those who are unprepared and unskilled. And yet she also knew that luck, like most things, cannot be truly missed until it i</i></span>
  <span id="freeText11519462693472690106" style="display:none"><b>For a bit of W.W. Hale eye candy go to</b> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://irresistiblereads.blogspot.com/2011/07/my-book-boyfriend-23.html#comments">http://irresistiblereads.blogspot.com...</a><br /><br /><b>Rating: 4.5</b><br /><br /><b>Favourite Quote:</b> <i>Luck is a strange thing in the life of any thief and halfway decent con man. What is it that keeps the mark from counting the till or the guards from looking up at precisely the wrong moment? Kat had learned at a very young age that luck is for the amateur, the lazy---those who are unprepared and unskilled. And yet she also knew that luck, like most things, cannot be truly missed until it is also truly gone.</i><br /><br />When it comes to sequels they can be a scary thing especially when you love the first book. But Uncommon Criminals is just as good as Heist Society. Once again Ally Carter offers all the right elements for another fun read - clever writing, a quick and suspenseful plot and entertaining characters.<br /><br />Again there were plenty of twists in this cleverly constructed plot making it impossible to put Uncommon Criminals down. And when I did I was thinking about all the ways Kat could possibly get herself out of trouble this time. I also love how Carter brilliantly describes the settings. She really knows how to capture the beautiful places like Monte Carlo the crew visits and you can picture everything perfectly thanks to Carter's wonderful writing. <br /><br />Kat is a genuine and likeable character. She is independent, smart and stubborn. In this instalment Kat has to learn to that she doesn't have to do everything on her own even if she doesn't need help. That it is okay to want help from her crew. Kat showed a lot growth. I also love the distinctive bunch of secondary characters. As soon as I started the book I was eagerly awaiting when Hale, Gabrielle, Simon or the Bagshaw brothers would pop up in the story and when they did they didn't disappoint.<br /><br />I know fans of the first book will be wondering about the romance. Does anything happen with Hale? Well all I can say is the spark is still there and you will have to read the book (I recommend immediately). <br /><br />Overall, this is one addictive series that I highly recommend. I really hope Carter writes a Heist Society #3.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11519462693472690106" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2167512300" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=3-star-read">3-star-read</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2167512300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16007112969115186231"><b>2.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I'm reading the reviews for this book and all I can say is that I definitely agree with many of you who said that this book is truly a YA book intended for <i>young adults</i>. I wish I read it when I was 14 or 15 because I would've adored it. It's light, fun and overall cute. Of course, sometimes we get a bit of drama-llama situations and questionable choices made by our interesting characters but overall, this entire trilogy is entertaining. Hale is cute, though, I love him.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_178355404" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178355404" />
    <a title="Nonie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2485441-nonie"><img alt="Nonie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1246648719p2/2485441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178355404?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nonie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nonie" href="/user/show/2485441-nonie">Nonie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178355404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16955143384192828864">There was no way I couldn't like this book even if I tried. Ally Carter wrote in everything I look for in a good heist story: the loyal crew for the hero (or in this case, heroine), plot twists at every turn, crazy mysterious villains, and of course, the seemingly impossible heist that the crew needs to pull off by the end of the story.<br/><br/>I would say that Uncommon Criminals is the blockbuster, popcorn novel for YA for this summer as Super 8 is this summer's blockbuster movie for Hollywood- sort of </span>
  <span id="freeText16955143384192828864" style="display:none">There was no way I couldn't like this book even if I tried. Ally Carter wrote in everything I look for in a good heist story: the loyal crew for the hero (or in this case, heroine), plot twists at every turn, crazy mysterious villains, and of course, the seemingly impossible heist that the crew needs to pull off by the end of the story.<br /><br />I would say that Uncommon Criminals is the blockbuster, popcorn novel for YA for this summer as Super 8 is this summer's blockbuster movie for Hollywood- sort of hyped up but not as much as others have been (and attached to several big names of their respective industries).<br /><br />Of course coming from Ally Carter, the plot of Uncommon Criminals was nothing short of riveting. For the whole 304 pages I kept the novel in my hands and never looked up unless to quickly take a sip of my caramel frapp, or occasionally getting distracted by people sitting next to me. The writing was elegant and polished, adding some glamor needed for the story like this.<br /><br />Kat was a believable character. The way she sticks with her family, and the way she takes up a Robin Hood-like role was poignant to me. She seems so wise and she's seen so much of the world already that I was taken aback when I remembered that she was only fifteen. The same goes for the rest of her crew. It's hard to believe that they're only sixteen (or under!) when they're country-hopping by themselves, but hey, it works.<br /><br />Speaking of Kat's crew, I badly badly badly want to join them. Not so much for the thievery, but for the traveling (I want to go all around Europe...) and working with the crew wouldn't be bad. The second in command of Kat's crew is W.W. Hale, who's handsome, smart, <i>(conveniently rich)</i>, and every bit as stubborn as Kat herself. One of the best aspects of the novel, besides the thievery was Kat and Hale dynamic. It plays out nicely because we (and Kat and Hale themselves) never forget that they're first and foremost best friends. <br /><br />The other crew members are Simon, the tech geek of the group (Q: Why is every "geeky" guy named Simon these days?); Angus and Hamish, the adorable brothers (note: every heist story needs a pair of brothers); and Gabriella, Kat's cousin and foil in the series meaning that she's fashionable and knows how to hold herself. <br /><br />The heist itself? Brilliantly done. I know that I'll have to read over the ending again to take in all of it. I'm really looking forward to finding out who Visily Romani is (or will we every find out?). It might've been the frapp and the windy weather outside, but it suddenly got chilly whenever Mr (or Ms?) Romani's name got mentioned. Very mysterious....*scratches chin* <br /><br />Uncommon Criminals can get serious sometimes as the themes of the story-family, friendship, betrayal- are serious, but it's always, just like any well-made Hollywood popcorn summer blockbuster, <i>fun</i>.<br /><br />Recommended to all. :) </span>
  <a data-text-id="16955143384192828864" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11024288435462528544">Ahhhh. Where do I begin?<br/>I remember reading Heist Society a loooong time ago, I remember listening to the audiobook of it quite a few times,<br/>I remember loving this series. I just didn't rememmber HOW MUCH.<br/><br/>I loved this book! I was so surprised and pleased to discovered it is as good as the first one, plus more adventures,<br/>more truths, even more lies, and oh so many incredibly kick-butt action!<br/><br/>The characters! Gosh the characters! I didn't recall them being this awesome! <br/>they were all SO CLEVER, SO SM</span>
  <span id="freeText11024288435462528544" style="display:none">Ahhhh. Where do I begin?<br />I remember reading Heist Society a loooong time ago, I remember listening to the audiobook of it quite a few times,<br />I remember loving this series. I just didn't rememmber HOW MUCH.<br /><br />I loved this book! I was so surprised and pleased to discovered it is as good as the first one, plus more adventures,<br />more truths, even more lies, and oh so many incredibly kick-butt action!<br /><br />The characters! Gosh the characters! I didn't recall them being this awesome! <br />they were all SO CLEVER, SO SMART. It takes some (okay, a lot) of talent to write a book like this, and to me,<br />Miss Carter deserves an standing ovasion! I can't even imagine how much time it took for her to plot all her characters' actions.<br />Each and everyone of the situations on this book were complicated and tricky at first to be ended later in the most simplified way you could think of<br />(or actually, haven't think of) these guys are teenagers after all, and trust them to find the answer to an exit problem using five hundred doves (not kidding, don't ask)<br /><br />What I also loved about this second book is that it shows Kat's flaws. I mean I knew she had them, SHE knew she had them,<br />but it's nice to see them aknowledged. She can be a super kick ass thief, but she's also a fifteen year old girl who has normal problems while living an extraordinary life.<br /><br />And Hale, oh W. W. Hale the Fifth, how I love you! He kept the loyalness he has come to be known for. He's awesome, you can tell he's deeply in love with Kat,<br />but he's not gonna take her crap, and I like that, he's fierce! reminds me of a GOOD Chuck Bass, utterly confident, careless in a way only the extra-rich are.<br /><br />Every other character kick major butt in this one too. Gabrielle was cool in book 1, but I LOVED her in this one. And Nick, oh Nick I love you too &lt;3<br />I just hope Miss Carter has something good prepared for him, cause in the short amount of pages he's been in, I've come to love him and wish him nothing but the best.<br /><br />This book is incredible and I can't wait for the people at WB to give the green light so they can start turning this series into a movie! <br />It'd be the ultimate action-packed, romance-full, funny-filled film I've ever hoped to watch!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2481098032152839732"><i>“Love is the biggest con of all”</i><br/><br/>This sequel is really better. I could totally picture the world and loved Carte's way of making the characters look like good badass people. They are thieves who have no unbelievable tech, guns or really dangerous people behind them and still made the book enjoyable. I liked how they were conning and robbing in a classic and elegant way and still were the good guy. And how sly they were. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435423848ra/15344729.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The writing was really easy and pleasant but the romance...<br/><br/><i>“Kat felt her hear</i></span>
  <span id="freeText2481098032152839732" style="display:none"><i>“Love is the biggest con of all”</i><br><br>This sequel is really better. I could totally picture the world and loved Carte's way of making the characters look like good badass people. <div id="review_338244324" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/338244324" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3947264-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389401312p2/3947264.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/338244324?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/3947264-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=action-packed">action-packed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=girl-power">girl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=love-geometry">love-geometry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=little-romance">little-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=plot-twist">plot-twist</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer338244324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3112797013113700358">I honestly thought that I would like this better than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6574102.Heist_Society__Heist_Society___1_' title='Heist Society (Heist Society, #1) by Ally Carter' rel='nofollow noopener'>Heist Society</a>, but the ending failed so miserably that I am left feeling nothing but disappointment. The ingredients for a fun, intelligent read were <i>there</i>, but they were wasted. Overall, the story was distractingly unrealistic, the characters were bland, and the ending was poorly put together.<br/><br/>First, let's talk about the novel as a whole. I am echoing myself from my review of the first book, but really? I'm supposed to believe these kids are </span>
  <span id="freeText3112797013113700358" style="display:none">I honestly thought that I would like this better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6574102.Heist_Society__Heist_Society___1_" title="Heist Society (Heist Society, #1) by Ally Carter" rel="nofollow noopener">Heist Society</a>, but the ending failed so miserably that I am left feeling nothing but disappointment. The ingredients for a fun, intelligent read were <i>there</i>, but they were wasted. Overall, the story was distractingly unrealistic, the characters were bland, and the ending was poorly put together.<br /><br />First, let's talk about the novel as a whole. I am echoing myself from my review of the first book, but really? I'm supposed to believe these kids are capable of huge, dangerous heists? They don't seem to put much thought into their plans, and after awhile it gets tiring to be <i>told</i> what brilliant young thieves they are when I haven't been successfully <i>shown</i> that this is true.<br /><br />There's also a lot of telling (instead of showing) when it comes to the characters. I have no emotional attachment to a single one of these people, probably because they never come alive to me. I don't even remember the Bagshaw brothers' names, let alone understand the differences in their personalities. (Because liking to blow stuff up <i>doesn't</i> count as a personality trait, FYI.) Even the two main characters, Kat and Hale, seem like your typical reader stand-in and vaguely dreamy love interest, respectively. <br /><br />Quick sidenote about Hale: I am so over this archetype. Overprotective, possessive dudes are running rampant in 95% of the teen fiction I've been reading lately, and I find 0% of them attractive. So Hale needs to either grow up or go away.<br /><br />However, despite all of these issues, the biggest problem for me was how weak the ending was. There were several plot-twists that occurred simultaneously, and none of them were executed well. I was irritated by how <i>impossible</i> the ending was-- impossible to guess, that is. I even went back and reread key scenes, but Carter neglected to lay even the most basic foundation to show how her plot-twists could happen. There were no subtle clues, no vague wording, to give any indication that the ending was even planned.<br /><br />And it really sucks that this is the case. Because up until the ending, I was moderately enjoying myself. These books are fast-paced and action-oriented, which is refreshing in the sea of emo romances dominating the YA section. If only Carter had put more thought and effort into wrapping up her plot (and I wouldn't mind more rounded characters, either), then this book might have been something.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3112797013113700358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4439004414344545467">Hmmmm. I didn't love this one as much as I loved Heist Society. Maybe because there wasn't much plot in my opinion? Until the crew arrives in Monte Carlo there are a few key scenes but most of the time is spent on Kat thinking she has it all cover all by herself and totally secluding her crew + not listening to anyone when they try to give her advice.   <span id="freeText4439004414344545467" style="display:none">Hmmmm. I didn't love this one as much as I loved Heist Society. Maybe because there wasn't much plot in my opinion? Until the crew arrives in Monte Carlo there are a few key scenes but most of the time is spent on Kat thinking she has it all cover all by herself and totally secluding her crew + not listening to anyone when they try to give her advice. Of course, she learns and grows throughout the novel, but I really struggled with being 100% supportive of Kat during the whole book. <br><br>My favorite character is probably Gabrielle and I adore the friendship the cousins are developing. Kat wasn't a huge fan of Gabrielle in the first book, but she slowly begun to realize that her cousin is in her corner and their relationship in Uncommon Criminals is really endearing. Speaking of relationships, I loooooooove the shippy feels! They're so great! It's not overpowering, but it's constantly there and I am fully on board (͠≖ ͜ʖ͠≖)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459497915i/18617263.png" width="400" height="347" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>OK SO I'M KINDA PISSED BECAUSE I SPENT A GOOD 15 MIN WRITING ABOUT THE PROBLEMS OF THIS BOOK AND THAT PART DIDN'T POST UGHHHHHHHHHHHH.<br><br>ANYHOW IN SHORT WHAT I SAID WAS:<br><br>1. THE VILLAIN WAS ANNOYING. She's only said to be this bad-a thief by EVERYONE but nothing is ever shown except <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[how she conned Kat <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. None of her jobs are talked about except that one job with <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Eddie &amp; Charlie <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and the other jobs are all like "oh she probably invented that trick" ummmmmmmm ok. So yeah I didn't really get the big bad part and found her more annoying than anything else tbh.<br><br>2. The whole Paraguay/Uruguay part was super annoying as well. Kat (and everyone else) is supposed to be this mastermind of all things and now you're telling me that she can't remember whether it's Paraguay or Uruguay? They're two different countries. If I was from one of them I'd be offended because that's probably what happens irl all the time that people just don't care enough to remember and to make it into a running joke that's supposed to be cute and quirky is not that appealing.<br><br>3. THERE IS NEXT TO NO INFORMATION STILL ABOUT ANYTHING! For instance ...<br><br>*is this a literal or figurative family? because as far as I know -- Simon and the Bagshaws aren't connected to Kat and Gabrielle through blood; also, there are quite a few uncles mentioned and we know pretty much nothing about them except 2.<br><br>*if not then how did Simon and the Bagshaws end up with "the family"?<br><br>*where are Kat's grandparents if Uncle Eddie and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Uncle Charlie <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> are her family but her grandparents aren't anywhere to be seen? From either side of the family. And same about Gabrielle since Eddie isn't her grandfather either.......<br><br>*what exactly happened to Kat's mom <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that lead to her death <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>? (this may have been said and I just don't remember)<br><br>*don't the other families ever want the same jobs that "our" family wants? do they try to take them? what kind of conflicts does this cause and does "our" family have families they are more close to? have there been any marriages or allegiances between some families? why haven't we seen any of those families?<br><br>There were more things but I just don't remember. As a whole I liked it and I laughed out loud quite a few times, but omgggg I have so many questions and none of them are answered. I'm not a huge fan of all these plot holes and lack of information on everything and especially the character backgrounds. I think these books could benefit from 20-30 more pages at least just to give some background and talk about the characters more in depth.<br><br>*you can see the graphic in HQ on my tumblr in this Heist Society graphic set <a href="http://cobaltrose.tumblr.com/post/142032476412/read-in-2016-heist-society-books-by-ally-carter" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/786797788" />
    <a title="rachel ☾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17290119-rachel"><img alt="rachel ☾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591333266p2/17290119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/786797788?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="rachel ☾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="rachel ☾" href="/user/show/17290119-rachel">rachel ☾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780734411938" href="/book/show/11932057-uncommon-criminals">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=mystery-thriller-suspense">mystery-thriller-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=young-adult-lit">young-adult-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17290119-rachel?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer786797788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13078937794099735493"><b>2.5 stars</b> <br/><br/>I wish I had more to say about this book. This is my third <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/56224.Ally_Carter' title='Ally Carter' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ally Carter</a> book (I've read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9948788.Heist_Society' title='Heist Society by Ally Carter' rel='nofollow noopener'>Heist Society</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/852470.I_d_Tell_You_I_Love_You__But_Then_I_d_Have_to_Kill_You__Gallagher_Girls___1_' title='I'd Tell You I Love You, But Then I'd Have to Kill You (Gallagher Girls, #1) by Ally Carter' rel='nofollow noopener'>I'd Tell You I Love You, But Then I'd Have to Kill You</a>) and so far I've found all her books kind of <i>meh</i>. But with the promise of teen art thieves, heists, cons, action, espionage, cursed jewels, ancient Egypt and Hale, I couldn't resist trying again. <br/><br/>But I almost wish I hadn't bother.<br/><br/>This book was just dull. None of the characters developed in the slightest since we last met them, a</span>
  <span id="freeText13078937794099735493" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars</b> <br><br>I wish I had more to say about this book. This is my third <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/56224.Ally_Carter" title="Ally Carter" rel="nofollow noopener">Ally Carter</a> book (I've read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9948788.Heist_Society" title="Heist Society by Ally Carter" rel="nofollow noopener">Heist Society</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/852470.I_d_Tell_You_I_Love_You__But_Then_I_d_Have_to_Kill_You__Gallagher_Girls___1_" title="I'd Tell You I Love You, But Then I'd Have to Kill You (Gallagher Girls, #1) by Ally Carter" rel="nofollow noopener">I'd Tell You I Love You, But Then I'd Have to Kill You</a>) and so far I've found all her books kind of <i>meh</i>. But with the promise of teen art thieves, heists, cons, action, espionage, cursed jewels, ancient Egypt and Hale, I couldn't resist trying again. <br><br>But I almost wish I hadn't bother.<br><br>This book was just dull. None of the characters developed in the slightest since we last met them, and I had the same problems with them that I did last time. We barely seem to see them at all! We see what they <i>did</i> and what their role in the various heists were, but we never got to sit back and really see <i>them</i>... which was annoying, obviously. I think this was mainly because of the weird writing style. <br><br>The writing purposely left a lot out or skipped over important scenes so that we wouldn't know what was happening and be surprised at the end. Well, you know what? I don't like feeling manipulated... especially when I know that I am being mislead on purpose. If you could have surprised me at the end, I would have loved it. But instead we <i>know</i> that everything isn't as it seems, and then it tries to spring it on us that everything was a ruse. Well, sorry if we all saw through that. It wasn't half-obvious or anything... *rolls eyes*<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380307185ra/688121.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anyway, I'm not exactly impressed but I am still interested to see how everything wraps up in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13580928.Perfect_Scoundrels__Heist_Society___3_" title="Perfect Scoundrels (Heist Society, #3) by Ally Carter" rel="nofollow noopener">Perfect Scoundrels</a>. I'm hoping we'll find out what the heck is up in Paraguay/Uruguay. Unless the rumours of a fourth book are true?</span>
  <a data-text-id="13078937794099735493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8463310297367856660"><i>Uncommon Criminals</i> is the second book from the <i>Heist Society</i>. I don't really know how I feel about it.. so many towards the end of this review I will know? Maybe?<br/><br/>Okay, so, this book was meh. Just like the previous book. I don't really know if I want to torture myself with more of these meh books but I haven't made my decision.. yet. Maybe they will get better or worse.. but I wont know until I read them. Maybe I'll flip a coin. <br/><br/>So this book was dull, boring, and again MEH. I still haven't really</span>
  <span id="freeText8463310297367856660" style="display:none"><i>Uncommon Criminals</i> is the second book from the <i>Heist Society</i>. I don't really know how I feel about it.. so many towards the end of this review I will know? Maybe?<br /><br />Okay, so, this book was meh. Just like the previous book. I don't really know if I want to torture myself with more of these meh books but I haven't made my decision.. yet. Maybe they will get better or worse.. but I wont know until I read them. Maybe I'll flip a coin. <br /><br />So this book was dull, boring, and again MEH. I still haven't really connected to the characters and I also haven't seen a lot of development between them either. I also don't really like the writing style. I'm pretty sure that's why I'm not really connecting to anything because we are only really seeing what they did but not what were doing throughout the whole book. It was annoying and frustrating to read. Does it change throughout the series? Does it get better? I have no idea.<br /><br />Besides the frustrating writing, I just feel like I either missed a shit ton of things happening.. or the author just skipped over things really quickly. Either thinking in it her head.. and thinking she typed it? I don't know but it happens - a lot, to me. <br /><br />Overall, I have no idea if I wanted to dive into the third book. I took a second chance on this series and I'm still not impressed, intrigued, or even slightly enjoying myself. I'm just numb to reading this series right now.</span>

<div id="review_1064354480" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1064354480" />
    <a title="Sara (Freadom Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24190242-sara-freadom-library"><img alt="Sara (Freadom Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590346455p2/24190242.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1064354480?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara (Freadom Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara (Freadom Library)" href="/user/show/24190242-sara-freadom-library">Sara (Freadom Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11424208-uncommon-criminals">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24190242-sara-freadom-library?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24190242-sara-freadom-library?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24190242-sara-freadom-library?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1064354480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer394424522414839500">Actual rating 4.5 stars<br/><br/>This review was originally posted at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://freadomlibrary.wordpress.com/'>https://freadomlibrary.wordpress.com/</a><br/><br/><b>Critically</b><br/>Plot – 4.5 out of 5 stars<br/>I enjoyed this sequel more than the first book. It was entertaining, fun and full of action. It’s full of suspense and twists and turns that I did not see coming at all. Thankfully, there’s more background information on the character’s and their family’s lives of thieving. This book focuses a lot on family and friendship but it has more of a romance as well.<br/><br/>Writing</span>
  <span id="freeText394424522414839500" style="display:none">Actual rating 4.5 stars<br /><br />This review was originally posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://freadomlibrary.wordpress.com/">https://freadomlibrary.wordpress.com/</a><br /><br /><b>Critically</b><br />Plot – 4.5 out of 5 stars<br />I enjoyed this sequel more than the first book. It was entertaining, fun and full of action. It’s full of suspense and twists and turns that I did not see coming at all. Thankfully, there’s more background information on the character’s and their family’s lives of thieving. This book focuses a lot on family and friendship but it has more of a romance as well.<br /><br />Writing Style – 4 out of 5 stars<br />The writing style is funny, simple and really easy to read. Honestly, I always fly through Ally’s books because they’re so entertaining and fun and sometimes even intense that I always want to know what’s going to happen next. It’s detailed, descriptive and fast paced. It has a third person POV most of the time from the main character but with also extra chapter with different character’s POVs which bring new and extra details to the story.<br /><br />Characters – 4 out of 5 stars<br />This improved so much more in this second book. One of my biggest complaints for the first book was the fact that we didn’t get enough background information on the character’s and their family and that is totally rectified in this book thanks to the plot. I definitely found myself connecting a bit more with all the different characters in part because I got to know them more through their relationships. It was just what I needed. Kat has grown from the first book but not necessarily in the best way. She’s gotten over confident and extremely independent. She’s stubborn and it causes a rift between her and the rest of her family… again. I’m glad she grew in this book as well toward a more humble attitude which aligns with her determination and makes this a great book to read. I was kind of upset with Hale in this book though I totally understood where he was coming from. He’s hurt and angry and he feels vulnerable. It was nice to see a more emotional side of him even if he still carries on with his charming and protective self. I feel like the side characters in this book didn’t have as much exposure as they did in the first book but again, there was a lot more family background information so I guess I can live with it.<br /><br /><b>Emotionally</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I definitely enjoyed this one more than the first book and I’m slowly but surely falling in love with this cast of characters.<br /><br />The plot is entertaining. It’s two months after the events of the first book and Kat has been traveling around the world pulling cons and heists on her own for a noble purpose. But she’s approached by an older woman and implored to steal one of the biggest gems in the world, even though it is cursed. But things don’t really turn out the way she wants them to. This book was a lot ore exciting and suspenseful than the first. The stakes are higher and the job is much harder than ones they have encountered before. It’s almost like a surreal setting and you want nothing more than for the characters to pull it off but every single facet is against them and what they’re trying to accomplish. There were quite a few twists and turns that I did not see coming at all which I really appreciated. Sometimes with these books, in this particular genre, things happen way too quickly or too conveniently to be believed (beyond the fact that teenagers are pulling off heists) and I loved that this book turned things on its head and left me floundering to see how they were actually going to get their shit together and pull off what they needed to do. These obstacles challenged the characters, specially Kat. They had to think outside the box and grow and learn together which made the story much richer. I loved getting to know more about the adults in the family and the way they’ve shaped the legacy the kids are now carrying on. Their history is so complex and intriguing so yes, I still want more and more about them and the main characters’ childhoods. Just everything about this group!<br /><br />Kat goes through a lot in this book. She’s become really independent. She’s spent the last few months pulling off cons and heists on her own which gives her a sense of superiority. She feels like she’s better than her family and not only that, that her reasons for doing what they do are also better. She’s cocky and a little bit self-righteous and that turned me off a bit though I can see how it would be a natural progression for her character. But luckily, she gets a really nasty dose of reality and begins to grow and change from that outlook. I’m glad it wasn’t something that happens overnight, old habits die hard and being independent for Kat is really hard to break. But she slowly begins to put more of her faith and trust in her family and what they can do together and it was really great to see.<br /><br />The side characters in this series are some of my favorite though they definitely took more of a backseat in this particular book. Hale is still my overprotective sweetheart. I’m really happy that we got to see more vulnerability and emotion from him. In the first book, he kind of got by on his charms and his jokes and while I love that, he needed more depth and it was obviously appreciated. Gabby is getting to me. Honestly, she has that kind of personality that generally annoys other girls because that’s just how we are. But we also get to see a different side of her in this series because of certain circumstances and she’s actually quite funny. The rest of the characters have their unique quirks and oddities and we also managed to see some other side to them which now that I think about is a direct effect of the plot and what it’s all about but I still really enjoyed it.<br /><br />Overall, I liked this book much better than the first one, the books are definitely getting better each time. The plot is exciting, entertaining and intense. It’s fast paced and kept me on the edge of my seat the entire time. There’s a lot of character development for the main character and I loved her growth from the first to the second book. We finally get some background information on her family and we get to see different sides to the other characters in the crew which was awesome. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="394424522414839500" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3632347773535055683">✭✭✭✬✩ <b>~ 3.75 Stars</b><br/><br/>This was really fun and enjoyable, but I'd say I didn't like it *quite* as much as I liked the first book. Just by a smidge.<br/><br/>Kat and her crew are back in <b>Uncommon Criminals</b>, and this time their mission is to steal the Cleopatra Emerald from a man named Oliver Kelly, whose grandfather stole it from an Egyptian tomb. This is the biggest job Kat has ever had: nobody has ever successfully stolen the Cleopatra before. And if that wasn't enough, the Emerald is also supposedly cursed, </span>
  <span id="freeText3632347773535055683" style="display:none">✭✭✭✬✩ <b>~ 3.75 Stars</b><br /><br />This was really fun and enjoyable, but I'd say I didn't like it *quite* as much as I liked the first book. Just by a smidge.<br /><br />Kat and her crew are back in <b>Uncommon Criminals</b>, and this time their mission is to steal the Cleopatra Emerald from a man named Oliver Kelly, whose grandfather stole it from an Egyptian tomb. This is the biggest job Kat has ever had: nobody has ever successfully stolen the Cleopatra before. And if that wasn't enough, the Emerald is also supposedly cursed, bringing misfortune upon anyone who comes in contact with it.<br /><br />It was a fun time! Kat &amp; Co are in Monte Carlo this time for the majority of the story, which means: casino scenes and ballgowns. Yes please. I've never been to Monaco but it's always kind of fascinated me - this tiny country the size of a town with a royal family, chock full of casinos and hotels. It's like another world.<br /><br />Unfortunately Kat did annoy me a <i>little</i> bit in this one, mostly surrounding everything to do with Hale. It annoyed me how he was always incredibly sweet and there for her and clearly loved her, and she kept insisting on her "I work alone" shit and taking Hale for granted. She also seemed to take sole credit for the heist in the previous book, when it was very clearly a team effort. <br /><br />Still, I do like her as a character, and I LOVE all the other characters. Hale is amazing. WHEN WILL WE LEARN HIS FIRST NAME???? Gabrielle is my girl crush, Simon is adorable, and Hamish and Angus are hilarious. <br /><br />Overall I'm really enjoying this series, I'm in love with the Art Thief Aesthetic, and any story with a heist is bound to have me hooked.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=concierge">concierge</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=library">library</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=audio">audio</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2987515211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13075948133139589910">Audiobook performed by Angela Dawe<br/>2.5** <br/><br/>Katarina Bishop is back with her crew of teen-aged thieves. In this second outing they are after the Cleopatra emerald, despite legend that it carries a curse. <br/><br/>There are a lot of twists and turns in this plot, and more than one intricate theft taking place. Not to mention cons and contra-cons. The relationship between Kat and Hale is on a continued slow-burn, but she seems disinterested for most of the book. Or perhaps she’s just so focused on her mission </span>
  <span id="freeText13075948133139589910" style="display:none">Audiobook performed by Angela Dawe<br />2.5** <br /><br />Katarina Bishop is back with her crew of teen-aged thieves. In this second outing they are after the Cleopatra emerald, despite legend that it carries a curse. <br /><br />There are a lot of twists and turns in this plot, and more than one intricate theft taking place. Not to mention cons and contra-cons. The relationship between Kat and Hale is on a continued slow-burn, but she seems disinterested for most of the book. Or perhaps she’s just so focused on her mission to … well, that would be spoiling the plot. Kat’s crew includes her cousin, the fabulously beautiful Gabrielle, as well as computer whiz Simon, and the Scots Hamish and Angus. And, of course, there are private jets, private yachts and the palace at Monaco to add color and interest. <br /><br />It's a fast read, and I like a lead female who is smart, determined and generally self-sufficient. But I didn't think it was as good as the first book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6574102.Heist_Society__Heist_Society___1_" title="Heist Society (Heist Society, #1) by Ally Carter" rel="nofollow noopener">Heist Society</a>. Still, I see the appeal for the target YA audience.<br /><br />Angela Dawe does a fine job performing the audio. She sets a good pace and clearly differentiates the many characters. I love how she voices Simon, who is suffering from a cold!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13075948133139589910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/433962596?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nitzan Schwarz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nitzan Schwarz" href="/user/show/8122395-nitzan-schwarz">Nitzan Schwarz</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer433962596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18338981752172503099"><a href='http://theafterwords.blogspot.co.il/2016/05/review-uncommon-criminals-ally-carter.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464187208i/19209926._SX540_.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><strong>
  <a href='http://theafterwords.blogspot.co.il/2016/05/review-uncommon-criminals-ally-carter.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>ORIGINALLY POSTED ON MY BLOG; </a>
  <em>
    <a href='http://theafterwords.blogspot.co.il/2016/05/review-uncommon-criminals-ally-carter.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>AFTERWORDS<br/><br/></a>
  </em>
</strong>So, if you read my review of <em>Heist Society</em>, <strong>you probably didn't expect me to pick up book two</strong>. I didn't think I'd do that, either. But then, while looking through my local bookstore, <strong>I found a hardcover copy of <em>Uncommon Criminals </em>and I just... thought it was so damned <em>pretty</em>. </strong>#Shallow<br/><br/><strong>I was hoping Uncommon Criminals might actually live to the potential of the awesome idea behind these books</strong>, but while it was a better read than the first, </span>
  <span id="freeText18338981752172503099" style="display:none"><a href="http://theafterwords.blogspot.co.il/2016/05/review-uncommon-criminals-ally-carter.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464187208i/19209926._SX540_.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><strong>
  <a href="http://theafterwords.blogspot.co.il/2016/05/review-uncommon-criminals-ally-carter.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ORIGINALLY POSTED ON MY BLOG; </a>
  <em>
    <a href="http://theafterwords.blogspot.co.il/2016/05/review-uncommon-criminals-ally-carter.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">AFTERWORDS<br><br></a>
  </em>
</strong>So, if you read my review of <em>Heist Society</em>, <strong>you probably didn't expect me to pick up book two</strong>. I didn't think I'd do that, either. But then, while looking through my local bookstore, <strong>I found a hardcover copy of <em>Uncommon Criminals </em>and I just... thought it was so damned <em>pretty</em>. </strong>#Shallow<br><br><strong>I was hoping Uncommon Criminals might actually live to the potential of the awesome idea behind these books</strong>, but while it was a better read than the first, it was by no mean anything incredible.<br><br><strong>Maybe Carter's writing is just not for me</strong> - a lot of people praise this book as an exciting and fast story. To me, the book was the complete opposite - it was a fast <em>read, </em>sure, but<strong> the content of the book felt slow and somewhat anticlimactic.</strong><br><br><strong>I did like Kat a whole lot more in this book</strong>. While she's always been likable, she's also been a flat character. In this installment, <strong>she's added more depth and felt a lot more rounded</strong>. She still lacked a past, but it wasn't as intolerable as in <em>Heist Society</em>.<br><br>Alongside Kat, <strong>Hale and Gabrielle get an upgrade in the depth department as well. </strong>Unfortunately, <strong>Simon and the brothers are left as the one dimensional decoration</strong> they were in <em>Heist Society </em>which sucks because I really like these characters. Far more than I like Gabrielle.<br><br>As for the <strong>romance</strong> - it was still <strong>such a small, undeveloped and unsatisfying part of the plot,</strong> but I <em>am </em>proud to say I'm <strong>Team Hale</strong>, and luckily (if I'm reading things correctly) he's also endgame, so yay for me! Though, I don't think my curiosity in that aspect is enough to make me read on with this series.<br><br><strong>One thing that really bothered me and drove me nuts were the heists themselves. Lots of parts were just left out and made no sense at all!</strong> Like, the Interpol. For god's sake, how did they make all these things explode? Or the doves and the casino. Maybe those are actually robot doves and that's why they did exactly what they wanted them to.<br><br><strong>I felt like Carter thought of all those interesting ideas for the heists, but had no idea how to explain them... so she didn't</strong>, believing the reader would just suck it up despite it. It may not bother everyone, but to me this was a major issue.<br><br>Maybe book three will be better. Maybe not. I'll probably never find out.<br><br><div>
  <a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-qYS_RE0ou6A/VlIzy5zTRCI/AAAAAAAAKPA/vi_mExUJJ6g/s1600/3%2Bstars.png" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458316766i/18472793.png" alt="" width="320" height="66" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><div>

    | 
  </a>
  <a href="http://theafterwordsblog.tumblr.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr </a>
</div><br><div></div><br><br>Old Version<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>To read this review and more pop by my blog <a href="http://drugscalledbooks.blogspot.co.il/2012/10/review-uncommon-criminals-by-alley.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Drugs Called Books</a></b><br><br>(This only looks like a long review cause I'm a space freak...)<br><br>If you would've asked me two weeks ago if I thought I was going to read this book anytime soon, I would've told you no. Heist Society did not impress me, and was a bit of a disappointment to me. <br><br>But then the most unbelievable thing happened; I found the book in my bookstore. Don't laugh, that's a truly unimaginable occurrence. Our bookstores are small and porely stocked when it comes to books in English, and I've never once seen the first book in the series. But there it was, sitting there, staring at me, looking all... pretty.<br><br>I truly love that cover. I don't know what it is about it that makes me love it, but I do.<br><br>And if that's not enough, it was in hardcover. Not the massive and heavy hardcovers we know, like Harry Potter and the Deathly Hollows or Bitterblue (which I have), but a hardcover just the right size. The kind of hardcover that makes you happy looking at it, that promises protection to the book's precious pages when you stuff it into your backpack to read in school.<br><br>Combine the cover and the hardcover and you have me, buying the book, hoping against all hope that this one in the series will be phenomenal.<br><br>Let me tell you something first; Heist Society was not a bad book. It was a light, fast read. But for me it was also a flat read. Perhaps it was the state of mind I was in at the time, but I never enjoyed it as others did. <br><br>But still, I bought this one. Because I love the idea of these books; young thieves, a female thief as a leader. The way it's handled is the part I'm less fond of.<br><br>This was a better read for me than the first. The main characters got more rounded, the plot more interesting. It wasn’t an amazing read, but it was nice.<br><br>Still, I’ve got a feeling Mrs. Carter’s writing is just not for me. I mean, I’ve read a lot of reviews saying how exciting and fast this book is. It’s a fast read. It’s not a fast story. Does that make any sense? It only took me a day to read this book, but the content of the book felt slow and somewhat anticlimactic. None of the parts felt truly “exciting” . I think it’s just an issue with me and Mrs. Carter’s writing. <br><br>Don’t get me wrong, her writing is by no means bad. It’s good. It just doesn’t generate the desired response from me. It doesn’t excite me, and left me feeling things moved rather slowly.<br><br>It saddens me that I don’t get as in love with it as others have, but that’s just life, I guess.<br><br>I did like Kat a whole lot more this book. She was always likable, but she felt flat to me on the first book. Here she had more depth. I still felt she lacked a past, but I could overlook it.<br><br>I’m totally Team Hale. I don’t even know why Nick is there, but I was glad [he never really stood as a love interest]. I mean, Hale and Kat are made for one another :]<br><br>And despite that… The relationship between Hale and Kat drove me crazy. I read this book mostly to know if they get together and when. It took a lot of time for that to happen, and I felt really unsatisfied. They acted just like friends for the most of the book, and I could not figure out if they were or weren’t an item by the end. Which might force me to read the next book. <br><br>The characters more developed in this book are Kat, Hale and Gabrielle. <br>Simon, Nick and the brothers are still pretty one dimensional, which is kind of sad because I really like Simon and the brothers. I think they're better than Gabrielle or Uncle Eddie, anyway. <br>I’m kinda wondering if something can happen between Simon and Gabrielle?<br><br>One thing that really bothered me were the heists themselves. Lots of parts were just left out, and made no sense.<br><br>For example, the theft of the stone was just simply too easy. But okay, never mind that. The Interpol. For god’s sake, how did they made all those stuff explode? Wouldn’t you have to already be in the building to do it? It made no sense!<br><br>Or the doves at the casino. How the heck did they manage to make them all fly into the casino? They did not release them in the casino, so how did they direct them.<br><br>I felt like Mrs. Carter thought of all those interesting ideas for the heist, but had no idea how to explain them; so she didn’t, trusting the reader would just make something up. That would not bother everyone; but it bothered me. A lot.<br><br>Anyway, I liked Uncommon Criminals better than Heist Society. It’s not amazing, but it was nice.<br><br>3 stars.<br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3637626786" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer995168940507496731">The 2nd book in the series. After reading the 1st look less than a month ago I wasn't expecting a lot from this one. However, this one wasn't slow like the first. I think because the characters had already been developed in the 1st book and we knew who they were and what to expect, somewhat. The 2nd book immediately took you right into the heist and kept you there the entire time. There wasn't a lot of breathing room, which I really liked as it kept my interest the entire time. I liked that it a</span>
  <span id="freeText995168940507496731" style="display:none">The 2nd book in the series. After reading the 1st look less than a month ago I wasn't expecting a lot from this one. However, this one wasn't slow like the first. I think because the characters had already been developed in the 1st book and we knew who they were and what to expect, somewhat. The 2nd book immediately took you right into the heist and kept you there the entire time. There wasn't a lot of breathing room, which I really liked as it kept my interest the entire time. I liked that it added in a little more romance and left with you wanted more enough to read to read the 3rd book in the series, which I plan to do. I want to see where it takes Hale and Kat. I will admit however, that I am still a little confused at this heist and con and not certain if I get what happened. The author has a great imagination of weaving a story. I will leave it at that and see you at the 3rd. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4rT3cnutINv8qyOQqYJfxoCAmXkVYrtt7ZgSxBdANsLYkp6gwPPps1uAl/Fed1UZVt9+sdvvNQq25lR12gPEWA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }
